text:
I made these while standing and chatting with a friend, and couldn't believe how fast they came together. (Couple beers had skewed my sense of time passage...) The taste is incredible. Made exactly as stated minus the nuts--boyfriend is allergic. No frosting needed! Sprinkled powdered sugar on top, more for looks than anything else. Everyone loved them. Just had one, couple days later, and they are still NOMMY! Update: Made these again with 'help' from my 5 year old. Still super tasty! Just wanted to add that I used about 1/4 c margarine and 3/4 light butter with canola oil, did not notice a change in taste or texture!

text:
Eggs make brownies cake-y and since we like chewy brownies, we used 2 eggs instead of 4, and 1 cup of flour instead of 1 & 1/2. We added 2 tsp of freeze-dried coffee to increase the complexity of the flavor, and created a mocha sensation: they were sensational! Chewy, rich, and moist. I'd definitely make these again -- esp. given how simple they are! Much better than boxed! Our brownies turned out chewy, moist, and chocolate-y!  P.S. We used a 7 x 11" pan, which worked really well.

text:
These were easy and very good.  Not quite as chocolatey as we like, but still very good.  Also, if you like your brownies less cakey, and more chewy, it's not the flour that does it, it's the eggs.  More eggs=more cake-like brownies; less eggs=chewier brownies.

These brownies were excellent! They are fast, easy and aren't messy. I only added one cup of flour (which is lucky because that's all the flour I had :D) and it came out really chewy and moist the way I love brownies. Also I added 1/4 cup walnuts but I wish I added more because they were great in these brownies. I will definitely make these again!   Update: I made these again and I forgot to mention that I did add 1 1/2 cups of white sugar and 1/2 cup of brown sugar, a tablespoon of instant coffee, 3 eggs instead of four and 2/3 cup of cocoa to up the chocolate flavor both times. I also baked for 25 min and they came out very soft and chewy.

text:
I've made these twice in two weeks, and here are my tweaks: used 1 & 1/4 cup flour and only 3 eggs, to reduce the 'cake-like' texture (oh, and 1/3 cup of that flour was whole-wheat: I try to sneak it into as much as I can:);I added 1 cup choc. chips; and, as I was making these I was on the phone (bad idea) and forgot to add the second stick of butter, so with only 1 stick & no additional oil or anything, they were really good- did not miss the extra butter!! Oh, and added 1 cup ground walnuts. Great brownies, and not as horrendously decadent as they might have been! 9/9/09 I make these every couple weeks now- so fast & easy! I discovered that adding a scant Tbls of instant coffee really kicks up the chocolate flavor. And, since some of my family don't like walnuts, I skip them and add 1 cup chocolate chips!

text:
This is definitely a five star brownie with a few adjustments. Like many of the other reviews I would suggest decreasing the flour to 1 cup if you want a chewy brownie. Also watch the bake time, I only baked mine for about 20 to 22 minutes. And don't over beat the mixture. I would beat by hand, adding the eggs one at a time, and would not use a hand/stand mixer. Made these last night and they came out chewy and fudge-like just how we like them.

I've made this recipe TWICE now - that's how good it is! The first time, I used an 8x8 glass dish and used all 4 eggs - it came out more like a CAKE. The second time, I used only 2 eggs and the suggested 9x13 glass dish - and it came out PERFECT :) The secret is in how many eggs/flour you use that makes the difference. For the second batch, I added walnuts and marshmallows for Rocky Road-style brownies and it was a hit :) This will be my go-to brownie recipe now!

This recipe was a huge hit tonight! I am not a baker by any stretch of the imagination and was hesitant to try "brownies from scratch". I'm so glad that I decided to try and that I found this recipe. I prefer a less cakey brownie, so followed the recommendation of a few others to cut the flour to 1c. I also used only .5c butter and substituted .5c applesauce for the rest of the better. Lastly, I prefer a thicker brownie, so I baked this in a 9x9 pan and increased the cooking time to 55 minutes. They turned out perfect. Thanks for the great receipe!

Wowza!  I am not an experienced baker, and rarely eat sweets.  Sometimes, though, I really want a Brownie.  Previously when that craving hits I bought a box mix at the grocery store.  Today I found this recipe and low and behold I had all the ingredients on hand.  After reading the reviews about the amount of flour making these too cake like and recommending cutting the flour to 1 cup I decided to compromise.  I didn't want too cake-ey or too gooey, so I made a guess and used a very heaping 1 cup of flour.  I used way more than 1/2 cup walnuts because I love nuts.  Also threw in some chocolate chips (that can never hurt I assume).  These are the Best Brownies I Ever Had.  Never will I buy a box again, these were just as easy and way way way better.

The brownies were moist, with good chocolate flavor and a nice dense texture. I used a glass 9x13 pan, and they were done in 30 minutes. text:
Excellent, quick and easy!  One word of caution as I just finished making my 3rd batch today for a youth function tonight...on the first batch, I was lazy and dumped all ingredients and THEN mixed with a wooden spoon.  Still tasty, but a totally different color and slightly different texture as the ingredients settled a little more unusually.  The last two batches, I mixed with a WHISK after EACH additonal ingredient.  Fantastic texture and rich chocolatey color!  It made a big difference whisking after adding each ingredient.  My husband is a very picky brownie eater and he tried one and said they were delicious!  No more brownie packages for me!  I also eliminated the extra 1/2 cup flour and used only one cup.

The first time I made this I cut back on the cocoa because most brownies are too chocolatey for my tastes.  Mistake!  The cocoa taste barely came through.  I made it again with the correct amount and they are perfect.  If you like things really chocolatey, I'd add some chunks of chocolate to the batter.

I freeze this batter in two 8x8 pans.  I bake from frozen and add about 8-10 minutes onto the cooking time.  I love having a pan in the freezer for last-minute potlucks, etc.

This is a really good brownies recipe! I love it because it used cocoa which I always have on hand and you don't need to melt chocolate. 

When I made them I found out I only had half of the number of eggs called for so I made it just with the ones I had on hand and they turned out great. I also iced them with a mixture of 3 tablespoons of melted butter mixed with 3 tablespoons cocoa powder, 1 tablespoon runny honey and half a cup of confectioners' sugar. My boyfriend thought they were delicous and they never last more than a day in our house!

text:
Ok, so it is after 1:00 am but I had to sit down and write this review. I had a box of store bought brownies in the pantry but really wanted to give these a whirl. Though brownies are not what anyone would call "healthy" I still like to control what is in the food I eat.  I appreciate that I knew exactly what went into these brownies. They took about 27 minutes in a 13 x 9. I let them cool for about 20 minutes before I cut them and they were heavenly! I am eating them as I type! I used one cup of flour instead of 1 1/2 cuz I like my brownies more fudge like. Besides that I followed exactly. After each ingredient I stirred to combine. Came out great! No more box brownies. I also like the ease of putting these together. No chocolate melting. The top doesnt look the same as box brownies when they are baking but they taste wonderful. Give em' a go! You probably have everything to make these already in your fridge/pantry.

text:
Very good! A few suggestions:  1. Use a 11x7 pan. A smaller pan makes thicker brownies.  2. Many users suggested lowering the flour amount to only 1 c so the brownies will be less cake-like. I suggest lowering it only to 1 1/4 c so they remain thick but adding 1/4 c vegetable oil to make them extra moist and more dense.  I can't decide whether the brownies are slightly TOO sweet. The 2 cups of white sugar creates a distinct, strong type of sweet. Next time I may lessen the white sugar to 1 1/2 c and then add some semi-sweet choc chips to compensate. I like rich, chocolaty brownies but I don't particularly like the ultra sugary flavor of white sugar.     Overall, I really like this recipe and will definitely use it again. It was quick, easy, and I LOVE that is uses cocoa instead of chocolate squares. I always have cocoa, so I can create these on a whim without having to plan ahead or run to the store.

text:
I've tried a lot of brownie recipes and usually I'm somewhat let down with the promised results. Not only are these simple to put together and bake, they turn out well, also. I halved the recipe and baked in an 8 inch glass Pyrex dish for about twenty five minutes, just until I could smell the aroma of baking brownie! I used a Dutch process cocoa (organic) and otherwise followed the directions. When they came out of the oven I placed some semi-sweet chocolate chips on the top and spread over the brownies as the chips melted, this formed a thin layer of icing that amped up the taste a bit. The texture was fantastic, sort of cake-y yet fudgy, yum. I can see where some may be let down by the mild flavor but this makes the recipe great for add-ins like nuts or flavored chips. Can't go wrong with this one!

text:
Even though I changed the recipe, I am giving this 5 starts.  Why?  Because it's the best recipe to start from.  If you like a cake like texture keep it as it is.  Read many of the reviews and it will be a snap to customize the recipe to get exactly what you want.  I took suggestions from a few reviews.  First I like very chocolatey, fudge-like brownies and since eggs make things "cake-like" reduced eggs to 2.  Reduced flour to 1 cup.  Increased cocoa to 3/4 cup.  Holy Cow!!  I'm in love! Can't wait to try again with the suggestion of adding instant coffee to increase the complexity of the flavor!  This was definitely the absolute easiest recipe ever!  OH!  And my tip to add - cut them when they're still warm for an even, more appealing looking cut.  Otherwise the crunchy outside breaks up.  They're firm on the outside and gooey on the inside.  (Because I used a smaller pan).

text:
I made these for co-workers over the weekend.  I made some changes like everyone, but the basis of the recipe is fantastic!  Everyone raved about them, so without further adieu...Here's my go to recipe for from scratch frownies. :)

1 c. Brown Sugar
3/4 c. White Sugar
1/4 c. Powdered sugar 
3/4 c. Cocoa Powder
1. tsp Vanilla
4 Eggs
1 1/2 Cups Flour
1/2 tsp. baking powder
1/2 tsp salt
1 C. Semi-Sweet Morsels

Melt butter, beat sugars for a few minutes, so the brown is well incorporated.  No one likes grainy brown sugar.  I followed the rest and scraped down the sides a few times in the kitchen aid.  Thanks again because it was my first time making scratch brownies and these were a HUGE hit!

Instead of walnuts I added a cup of semi sweet chocolate chips. After pouring the batter in the pan I topped it with a cream cheese topping...this is the topping (trust me it takes this brownie to a whole nother level:
8 ounces cream cheese, softened
1/4 cup sugar
1 egg
1/8 teaspoon vanilla extract
Mix it all together in a separate bowl and pour over the top swirling it into the brownie batter.

These were sooo decadent!

text:
I've never made brownies before, but decided to give this a try end of last week and i'm glad i did because they're delicious and my husband loves them! He wants me to show him how i make it some time!
I only used 1 cup of flour after reading other reviews and I used 1 teaspoon of honey instead of vanilla extract, as I didn't have any, plus being a Muslim, there may be ingredients in vanilla extract that may not be permissible for me to use. My only complaint is that despite baking it at 350 degrees Fahrenheit, it took 50 minutes to bake. 
Next time, i'll half the recipe since only me and my husband will be eating it (there were plenty of leftovers and there still are!), but it's a very easy recipe and i'm glad i found it! This is the first recipe i've tried out on here! Will hopefully try out more!
Update: made this again today after a chocolate cake broke apart when taking it out of the cake tin (no idea why!), but halved the quantity and left out the nuts which made a big difference to the taste and texture! It was more chocolatey and fudge-like, whereas last time it had more of a cake-like texture. My brother in law said, 'oh my God this is amazing!' and he actually thought I made it differently! My husband hasn't tried them yet, but I know he'll prefer the brownies this time too, although he did love the ones with nuts as well. This one's definitely going in my recipe book!

text:
This was a good, basic recipe. I only added 1 cup of flour like the other reviewers said, added 1/4 cup extra coco powder and used chopped semi-sweet bakers chocolate instead of nuts.. however, I cooked them in a cupcake pan for individual portions. I ended up having enough for two batches, 12 in the first and 6 in the second. The first batch ended up like cupcakes in both taste and texture, the bottom was also slightly over cooked. The the 6 remaining I decided to  reduce the heat to 300. The 6 turned out more like brownies than the first 12. Since I was making them for a birthday party, I decided that another batch was needed and I decided to change the recipe even more. I added 1 tbs of canola oil and 3 ounces of bakers chocolate, along with more 1/4 cup more coco powder. OMG... so good and so moist!!!

city:

country:
None
text:
I was making these for a Super Bowl party, and these are definitely better than Brook's Bombshell Brownies, but I think I will still search for a different recipe.  The first batch I made turned out wrong.  The cocoa powder in the batter balled up.  I went ahead and baked them to see how they would be, and they are edible, but I left them for my family to eat.  The second batch I tweaked to try and avoid that problem with the cocoa powder.  Here's what I did:  I used 1/2 c. butter and 1/2 c. applesauce.  I beat that in with the sugar, and then beat the 4 eggs and vanilla extract into the mix.  In a separate bowl I combined the cocoa powder, salt, 1 c. of flour, and the baking powder.   I stirred the dry ingredients together, and then gradually added it into the wet ingredients.  There were no lumps, and then I baked it in the oven for about 40 minutes.  They came out fine, but they're nothing spectacular.  For my own personal preference, I would make these a day ahead of time because they seem to get fudgier tasting overnight.

text:
These brownies were delicious and QUICK to make. I already had the ingredients on hand. I did do a few extra kicks to it, I used 3 instead of 4 eggs so the batter wouldn't be so cakey as others (Grab 2 small mixing bowls). In one small mixing bowl soften 1-8oz pkg of cream cheese, mix it with 1cup powder (confectioners)sugar, 1-egg and 1-teaspoon of Vanilla extract. In the other bowl take 1/2 cup of peanut butter (add apx. 1 1/2 to 2 tsp of softened butter, to help with the spreading consistentcy.) By the teaspoonfuls drop on top of the brownie batter that is in baking pan, alternating cream cheese filling with peanut butter one. take a butter knife or skewer (which ever is avl.) and swirl it through the brownie batter.  I recommend going straight down the long way about 5x's, then 6x's width wise. It's DEEELICIOUS!!! It's like a choc. cream cheese & Peanut Butter brownie all in one! My sons & husband loved them!!! I made it for or small Superbowl 44 home gatering but, with 2 teen an adolecent and Husband, there was not much to share with friends and family when they stopped by. (They did wrap up one for our Pastor. Thank GOD :D!) Don't double the receipe all at once. Make one batch then another. (The consistency of this batter you don't want to try doubling up front. The sugar crystals in the batter will make you think something didn't come out right but, it bakes just fine. If you add the toppings I suggested up your cooking time about 10-12 more mins.) ENJOY!!!

text:
I followed the suggestions from other reviewers and cut down the flour to 1 cup and added a tablespoon of sour cream.  I am not a chocaholic, but I found them lacking in chocolate flavor.  Also, the first bite tasted surprisingly eggy.  This is a cake-like brownie. I hadn't really thought about it, but I think I discovered I prefer a more dense brownie.  This is no fault of the recipe; just a personal preference.  If I had left the recipe as written, it probably would have been more dense, but it still wouldn't have been chocolatey enough for us.  Nevertheless, it's nice to have a simple recipe you can pull out of your hat in a moment's notice.  So, I probably wouldn't make them again....but I'm sure this recipe would suit lots of people just fine.

text:
I figured since I make these all the time I should probably review the recipe.  So easy and so quick!  They always disappear before they are completely cooled.  I line my pan with parchment paper so that I don't have to grease the pan... or clean it either!  Mine always take about 28 minutes to get that balance of cakey and chewy.  I am not sure why other reviewers struggle with the recipe.  It is extremely straight forward.  The "cakeyness" that some complain of is probably due to the type of flour they are using as well as the method they use to measure it.  Densely packed flour will quickly turn this into a cake.  Also, the better the cocoa powder (not hot chocolate mix!) the better these are.  Invest in your stomach and spoil your taste buds with some quality dutch cocoa and you will never go back to another recipe or store bought mix again.

I added chocolate chips, but they all fell down to the bottom, thankfully they didn't burn, since I had to increase the cooking time. This is my first attempt at making brownies from scratch, and as of right now, boxed brownies mixes are winning. I may fiddle around with a few other recipes, but I doubt I'll return to this one. My brother and I had a good time making them though, thanks.

text:
I made these for my husband, 14 year old and her boyfriend and they loved them.

I made them exactly as the recipe called for using my Kitchen Aid mixer, except I omitted the nuts abd at the end I melted 3 tablespoons of deulce de leche (used President's Choice brand) for 3 seconds in the microwave.  I made a grid with lines of the melted caramel across the top of the mix (poured into the pan) and then swirled them around with a knife. 

I greased the pan well with Crisco and then baked them for 30 minutes and they came out perfectly. 20 minutes is not long enough.  

The brownies came out beautifully moist and soft - the caramel I used worked really well. They're quite light, like a cake almost and aren't as rich, chewy or chocolatey as a store-bough brownie.  They are really nice, however, and I will make them again.

I prefer my brownies thick and chewy, so I altered it to 3 eggs and 1 1/4c flour, then baked in an 8x8 pan. It takes about 40 minutes to bake but is worth every tantalizing second. I have been bombarded with requests for the recipe.

Thanks for sharing!

text:
When I read "cakelike" brownies, I thought I wouldn't like them.  But, oh yes, they are so good!  They are less dense, but still rich.  I made a half recipe in a 9 X 9, used pecans instead of walnuts - and stuck some peanut butter chips and butterscotch chips in one side.  Tried some powdered frosting on some, too.  I was surprised at how moist they stayed overnight, too.  I'm made them earlier this week and I'm making another 1/2 batch again tonight.  
These take about 10 minutes to throw together - put the butter in the microwave on defrost for a couple minutes while you gather the rest of the ingredients.  I will never buy another box again - they have trans fats (partially hydrogenated oils and/or shortening) in them.  These are still fattening, but not as bad as box mixes.  
YUM!!

text:
These were fantastic!  I cut out the walnuts, but added about 1/2 cup of chopped dark chocolate (I just happened to have some on hand, and this was a good way to keep me from snacking on it) to the butter mixture after it was removed from heat. Definitely underbake these: I was at 24 minutes - they seemed raw at first, but a couple of hours later and on into the week they are perfect and moist.  There's nothing worse than an overbaked brownie!  I'll be using this recipe agan.

These are so easy to make.  Very good results. Especially good if you need a quick dessert as you probably have all the ingrdients at home.  The only change I made was to add a cup of chopped walnuts to the batter.  My only suggestion is to watch the timer carefully so that you do not overbake them. These are delicious!!

We like that it isn't sickeningly sweet.  Def more of a cakey consistency.  Mine baked for 25 min which was great.  Next time I think I might try increasing the cocoa powder in it.  It's a very flexible recipe - would be fun to try with chocolate chips, bits of caramel, peppermint chunks, etc.

text:
I was hoping this would be a  cakey brownie recipe.  When read the reviews where people said they cut back on the flour so it WOULDN'T be cakey, I decided to stick to the original recipe, except for adding another 1/4 cup of walnuts, since I like a nuttier brownie.  I baked it in a 9 x 13 pan for 20 minutes at first, but it needed a total of 30 minutes for the knife to come out clean.  That's pretty quick as far as I'm concerned.   

I did mix the ingredients a little differently than shown in the video.  I combined the sugar and cocoa powder, then added the melted butter, then the vanilla and eggs.  I combined the flour, salt and baking powder in a smaller bowl like most recipes recommend before adding it to the wet ingredients.  I added the walnuts after the flour mixture was combined with the wet ingredients.  I wanted to prevent any dry flour from sticking to the walnuts.  I was happy with the results and would make it again!

text:
Delicious! Thank you for sharing your recipe and thank you for all the reviews. Like many otgers, I modified the recipe to our liking. 4 star because of modifications but to be fair I never did try the original recipe. 

My modifications: Used a half cup of butter and a half cup of pureed avocado instead of the full cup of butter, reduced flour to 1 cup, used 2 instead of 4 eggs, reduced sugar to 3/4 cup white and 1/2 cup brown instead of 2 cup of white, 2/3 cups cocoa powder instead of 1/2 cup, and I added chocolate chips. Baked for 25 minutes. I was afraid it was going to be too thin therefore be too dry but it was so chocolatey and moist.  Because of the chocolate chips, I will reduce the sugar even more next time.

text:
I have a diabetic celiac at home and this recipe was one of the most easily adaptable I found. I removed the walnuts because I didn't have any handy. It turned out pretty well. I used a mix of three different gluten free flour: potato, cassava thick grain and rice. Next time I think I'll substitute out the cassava thick grain for cornflour to make it smoother. Also, I think I'll reduce the amount of flour by a fifth. It became quite thick, but the flavor is really good and it is a much better alternative than buying preprocessed every time.

text:
So easy to make.  First time making brownies from scratch.  I followed recipe with making some minor adjustments. Used 1 and half cups of sugar. It was fine for me but  hubby prefers a little more sweet. Next time will use 1 and 3/4 cups of sugar. Used 1 1/2 tsp vanilla and a tad over 1/2  cup of unsweetened cacao powder.  I also added half cup of walnuts.   Baked in a 9x9.5 pan for 30 minutes.   Lined pan with greased parchment paper. Came out of pan and off paper, easy peasy.  We like cake style brownies.  We enjoyed taste and texture and will use this recipe again.  Thanks for sharing.

Next time, I think I will reduce the butter as well because I thought they came out a little too oily.  My son couldn't wait, so we let these cool for a bit and ate the first ones while still warm.   You need to let these cool completely before eating, otherwise they taste very buttery.  They are perfect when cool.

I chose this recipe because my young daughter wanted to bake brownies and I thought it would make for a good beginner recipe.  She stuck to the recipe and was able to make them perfectly, with ease.  I love that these ingredients are always in my pantry/fridge.  My brownie recipe calls for two kinds of melted chocolate, a double boiler and carefully combining melted chocolate with eggs without scrambling them, she didn't need to deal with all of that. I must admit that mine tastes a bit better, which is why I gave this recipe 4 stars.  I'm an experienced baker and cook with many years under my belt and have learned to really taste food.  My husband, daughter and a few other friends absolutely loved and devoured these brownies which is also why I gave it 4 stars.  If you're looking for homemade brownies that are delicious, quick and easy this is a great recipe!

This is closest to boxed brownies that I've ever made--after decades, the search is finally over! I love that it only requires cocoa instead of chocolate pieces. It's a relatively flexible recipe, allowing me to use 1/2 applesauce/butter and a mix of white and whole wheat flour (I use roughly a 70/30 ratio).

text:
I've made this recipe a half dozen times or so now and have discovered some things that helped me.  First, I didn't change the recipe at all, other than leaving out the walnuts.  When I made the batter, I made it one ingredient at a time -- added butter to sugar, mixed well, added next ingredient, mixed well, and so on.  This totally changed the taste of the finished brownies -- SO MUCH better tasting!

There are definitely a cake-like brownie, not a fudgy brownie.  But, that's what I was looking for and what we like the most.

Great recipe!

I didn't listen to the flour suggestion but I did substitute butter since I didn't have enough on hand. Instead I used 189 ml of canola oil and 47 ml of water.    I also added a vanilla glaze using powdered sugar, a little butter, milk and vanilla. You put it on when the Brownies are warm, let them sit in the fridge for 5 minutes to let it harden, and voila! They came out a bit lighter and a perfect texture. Not too heavy and not too cakey.

text:
I am terrible at making brownies, but this recipe was very easy to follow. The batter came together in under ten minutes. I reduced the flour by about half a cup as suggested by other bakers and the brownies came out very moist and tasted great.


Tips and Tricks:
If you have a habit of overbaking your brownies like me, instead of greasing the pan line it with parchment paper to prevent  the brownies from sticking, and bake the brownies for 20 minutes uncovered then an addition 20 minutes (depending on your oven- mine in notoriously unreliable for even heating) covered with foil.  The brownies lift out of the pan without sticking and will be fully baked but remain moist and fudgy.

Quick and easy! I reduced the sugar to 1 cup brown sugar + 1/4 cup white sugar as I don't usually like very sweet desserts, used dark cocoa powder, and reduced the flour to 1 cup as per the helpful comments here :) Mixed by hand with a whisk, baked it for 25 mins, it was moist and not sickly sweet-- perfect with a scoop of ice cream! Will definitely make this again, maybe with less butter and baking it for about 22 mins instead. Thank you for the recipe!

text:
First time I made this recipe: I did as the other reviewers said and used 1 cup of flour opposed to 1 1/2. I also omitted 1/2 cup of walnut halves and instead added milk chocolate chocolate chips (about a handful). I didn't add the 1/2 teaspoon of salt since I used half unsalted butter and half margarine (which is a bit salty). The rest of the instruction I followed precisely as they were on the given recipe. I baked the brownies for exactly 45 minutes and they came out absolutely delicious.
Second time I made this recipe: I used an 8inx8in pan. I didn't use any measuring utensils but here are the estimates. I used about 3/4 flour, however, I feel I should have used 1/2 flour. I used 1 cup sugar. Instead of butter I used coconut oil, 1/2 cup. 3 eggs, however, I feel I should have used 2 eggs. 1/4 cup cocoa powder, 1/4 teaspoon baking powder, 1/2 teaspoon vanilla extract. No salt. No nuts or chocolate chips. I baked for 23 minutes, however, I feel I should have baked for a couple minutes less. With this one I felt the brownies came out cakey. Next time I make this in an 8x8 pan I will add less flour (1/2 cup) and one less egg (2 eggs). The brownies were also a bit coconuty (which I don't mind but family does) so instead I will go back to using real butter since I think it gives it a more brownie like taste. Apart from that this recipe is great. I've tried a few other recipes from this site (exact: no alterations) and none can compete with this one.

Easiest recipe ever!  I followed the recipe exactly as is written, and the brownies came out delicious.  My son took them to school as his birthday treat for his classroom.  The brownies were moist and chocolatey.  If I wanted them more chocolatey, I wouldn't reduce the flour -- I would add chocolate morsels.  I took me thirty minutes to produce the final product.  Ten minutes combining ingredients, and 20 to bake it.  I didn't add the nuts because not all kids like nuts.  I plan on using this recipe for brownies when I make my brownie/ice cream/hot fudge dessert.

None
text:
I gather the reviews that suggest adding extra cocoa powder for a darker, more chocolatey brownie were using a light grade of cocoa powder. Cocoa powders are graded by their % fat; we used a 20% cocoa powder (a "rich cocoa" grade) and 3/4 cup. The brownie batter is extremely dark and tasted very, very chocolatey. We also reduced the# of eggs from 4 to 3, using extra large eggs, to make them more fudgy and less cakey, and baked them in a 13 x 9 inch glass dish.

They came out very cakey even with 3 eggs vs 4, chocolatey, and light (weight and texture, not color). Will try next time with 1 cup of flour and 2 eggs to get a more fudgy consistency.

Very, very fast and easy with a kitchen aid mixer.

I just made these and snuck a piece to make sure they're okay before I bring them to a family event. ;)
I reduced the flour to 1 cup as other reviewers suggested and I also added a handful of semi-sweet choc. chips.  The bake time was longer than expected... my oven isn't the most powerful so at first I put them in for 27 mins. then another 4 and then an additional 4..! The texture of these brownies is great. Not too soft and not too fudgey. I'd add more choc. chips or something because the chocolate taste is a bit lacking. These are a good base brownie. I'm going to make these again and again and experiment by adding different ingredients! The title doesn't lie, these are super easy.

text:
I needed a recipe for brownies that was quick, easy, and preferably used cocoa as opposed to baking chocolate. Following this recipe, and the advice of other reviewers to reduce the amount of flour to one cup, yielded brownies that were rich and fudgy. The thin crust complemented the soft, dense texture, and the slightly bitter undertones of the chopped walnuts provided a nice balance to the sugar, as well as supplying crunch . 

Surprisingly, these brownies are not overly sweet, and a dusting of confectioners sugar added a perfect - and simple - flourish.

I used a 9x13 pan as the recipe recommended and found that the brownies were the perfect thickness. Baking took 20 minutes.

This brownie tasted good, but was too crunchy on the top and edges for me.  I ended up baking it for close to 45 minutes at the temp recommended.  After reading the reviews I reduced the flour to 1 1/4 cups (I like cake-y and my husband likes fudgey - good compromise) and I added about 1 cup of mint chocolate chips and used pecans instead of walnuts.  My husband really liked this recipe, so I may try again, adjusting for high altitude (I live at about 6000 ft) and adjusting the temp a bit.  I really enjoy brownies from a box, so I'm going to continue to search for a recipe that's more similar to that taste.  But good homemade recipe!

These brownies were terrific, but I did make a lot of changes from reading the reviews.  By changing them, they tasted fudgey with a top you normally get while making brownies. text:
I didn't have any brownie mix so I decided to see how hard it would be to make them homemade since I have never made them before. I cam across this recipe and read the reviews and decided it was very easy. I poured some of my batter into a smaller cake pan and the rest into a mini muffin pan. The mini muffins only took 10 mins. and the pan took 18 mins. and they were delicious. My whole family loved them and I made the recipe just as it is. They had a great flavor and texture.I will continue making these for our family.

text:
You named these perfectly, because the brownies WERE quick and easy to make.  I'm 25, a mother of 2, a chocoholic and brand new to this homemade cooking thing!!!  I felt like I owed it to my kids to make special treats for them from scratch.  It was time I learned, and this recipe was the perfect start.  For basic brownines, these came out just as good as the store bought mix.  I added a little vanilla extract and crushed m&m's for fun, but otherwise, followed the recipe.  I love how chewy they are, not dried out, not burnt, yet they held their shape nicely.  They didn't fall apart, so need for plates.  Just let them cool, cut in squares and eat out of the pan!!!  (Yes, they were that good  =) )  Thanks so much for helping to make my 1st "from scratch" project go so smoothly.  I would like to find a recipe that makes them come out more fudgy, but again, this is the perfect basic brownie recipe.
